--------------------------------------------------
Alright, so I've got this problem here about firefighters doing a "fill the boot" fundraiser. Their goal is to raise $6300. After the first 3 hours, they've raised $2100. The question is asking how many hours they have to fundraise in total to reach their goal, assuming they raise an equal amount each hour. The answer is supposed to be 13, but let me think through this step by step to make sure I understand why.

First, let's break down the information given. The total goal is $6300. After 3 hours, they've raised $2100. The question is asking how many more hours they have to fundraise in total to reach their goal, assuming they raise an equal amount every hour. $2100 / 3 = $700 per hour.

Okay, so they make $700 each hour. Now, their total goal is $6300, and they've already raised $2100. So, the amount they still need to raise is the difference between the goal and what they've already raised.

Let me calculate that: $6300 - $2100 = $4200.

So, they need an additional $4200. Since they raise $700 each hour, I need to find out how many hours it will take them to make $4200 at that rate.

Calculating that, 4200 / 700 = 6.

Okay, so the local firefighters are doing a "fill the boot" fundraiser, and their goal is to raise $6300. Hmm, that's quite a sum! After the first 3 hours, they've already managed to raise $2100. Now, I need to figure out how many more hours they have to fundraise in total to reach their goal, assuming that they raise an equal amount each hour. The answer is supposed to be 13, but let me see how that works step by step.

Alright, so let me break it down. The total goal is $6300, and they've already raised $2100 in the first 3 hours. To find out how much more they need to raise, I can subtract the amount they've already raised from the total goal. So, that would be $6300 minus $2100. Let me calculate that: 6300 minus 2100 is 4200. So, they need an additional $4200.

Now, the question is, how many more hours do they need to work to raise $4200, assuming they raise an equal amount each hour? Let me denote the number of additional hours they need as 'h'. Each hour, they raise the same amount, so I can assume that amount is constant. Let me call that amount 'r' for "rate" per hour.

Amount needed = Total goal - Amount raised so far

- $2100
--------
$4200

So, if they raise, say, $x each hour, then the number of hours needed would be the amount needed divided by their rate.

But wait, I don't know their rate yet. Maybe I can find that from the first 3 hours.

Rate = Amount raised / Time

Rate = $2100 / 3 hours

Calculating that:

$2100 divided by 3 is $700 per hour. So, each hour, they raise $700.

Okay, so now that I know their rate is $700 per hour, I can figure out how many hours they need to raise the remaining $4200.

Number of hours = Amount needed / Rate

Okay, so the firefighters are doing a "fill the boot" fundraiser and their goal is to raise $6300. After the first 3 hours, they've already raised $2100. They want to know how many more hours they need to fundraise in total to reach their goal, assuming they raise an equal amount each hour. The answer is supposed to be 13, but I want to figure out why.

First, let me break down what I know:

- Total goal: $6300
- Money raised after 3 hours: $2100
- They want to know the total hours needed to reach the goal, assuming equal raising each hour.

So, I think I need to figure out how much more money they need to raise after the first 3 hours and then determine how many hours at the same rate will get them to the total goal.

Let me write this down step by step.

--------------------------------------------------
Okay, so the problem is about firefighters doing a "fill the boot" fundraiser where their goal is to raise $6300. After the first 3 hours, they've already raised $2100. --------------------------------------------------
Okay, so there's this problem about the firefighters' boot fundraiser. They need to raise $6,300 in total. After the first three hours, they've already made $2,100. The question is, how many more hours do they need to work to reach their goal, assuming they raise the same amount each hour. And apparently, the answer is 13 hours. Hmm, I should figure out why.

Let me break it down. They have a goal of $6,300. They've already raised $2,100 in the first three hours. So, how much more do they need? I think I need to subtract what they've already made from the total goal. That makes sense because if they've already raised part of it, they just need the remaining amount.

So, subtracting $2,100 from $6,300... Let me do that: 6,300 minus 2,100. Hmm, 6,300 minus 2,000 is 4,300, and then minus another 100 is 4,200. So, they need an additional $4,200.

Now, they need to raise $4,200, and they're assuming they raise the same amount each hour. So, if I figure out how many hours it takes to raise $4,200 at a constant rate, that should give me the answer. Since rate is amount divided by time, and they want to know how much time for a given amount, it's amount divided by rate.

But in this case, since each hour they raise the same amount, the amount per hour is $4,200 divided by the number of hours they work. But wait, actually, since they already worked for three hours, and the rate per hour is $2,100 divided by 3, then the rate is $700 per hour. Let me confirm that: 2,100 divided by 3 is 700. So, each hour they raise $700.

Therefore, to find out how many more hours they need to raise $4,200, I can take the remaining amount and divide it by the hourly rate. So, 4,200 divided by 700. Let's calculate that: 4,200 ÷ 700.

Okay, so I have this problem about firefighters doing a "fill the boot" fundraiser. They want to raise $6300 in total. After the first 3 hours, they've already raised $2100. The question is asking how many more hours they need to fundraise to reach their goal, assuming they raise an equal amount each hour. The answer is supposed to be 13, but let me think through this step by step to make sure I understand why.

First, let's make sure I understand the problem correctly. They have a total goal of $6300. After 3 hours, they have $2100. We need to find out how many additional hours they need to work so that, when you add the money they've already raised to the money they'll raise in those additional hours, they reach $6300. And importantly, each hour they spend fundraising, they raise the same amount. So, it's a linear situation, right? The amount they make each hour is constant.

So, let's break it down. The total amount they need is $6300. They've already got $2100 after 3 hours. So, how much more do they need? I think I should subtract the amount they've already raised from the total goal. Let me write that down:

Total goal: $6300
Money raised so far: $2100
Remaining amount needed: $6300 - $2100

Let me compute that: 6300 minus 2100. Hmm, 6300 minus 2000 is 4300, and then minus 100 more is 4200. So, they need an additional $4200.

Now, we need to figure out how many hours it will take them to raise $4200 at the same rate they've been going. Since they raise an equal amount each hour, we can essentially calculate how much they make per hour and then see how many hours it'll take to make up the remaining $4200.

But wait, maybe there's a smarter way without calculating the rate per hour. Let's think about it another way. The amount they have left is $4200, and each hour they make the same amount. So, if I denote the amount they make each hour as "x," then:

Number of hours needed * x = $4200

But we don't know x yet. However, we do know that in the first 3 hours, they made $2100. So, if 3 hours give them $2100, then each hour they must be making:

x = $2100 / 3 hours

Computing that: 2100 divided by 3 is 700. So, they make $700 each hour.

Wait, let me verify that. If they make $700 each hour, then in the first 3 hours, that would be 3 * 700 = 2100, which matches the given information. Good, so that's correct.

Now, since they need to raise an additional $4200, and they make $700 each hour, the number of hours needed would be:

Number of hours = $4200 / $700 per hour

Let me calculate that. 4200 divided by 700. Hmm, 700 * 6 is 4200, right? Because 700 * 5 is 3500, and 700 more would be 4200. So, 6 hours.
